Bioinformatics. 2005, 21 (Suppl 1): i351-i358. 10.1093/bioinformatics/bti1018." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1944">67</a>] with default parameters except “--thresh = 10” for “filter-stage-2” step (additional 7.2% of genome were masked giving 5,722,364 bp out of 43,366,824 bp in total). After repeat masking, contigs were subject to independent gene prediction with four different approaches. First, we used GENEWISE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Birney E, Clamp M, Durbin R: GeneWise and Genomewise. Genome Res. 2004, 14: 988-995. 10.1101/gr.1865504." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1947">68</a>] to predict genes in loci which are similar to <i>Mimulus guttatus</i>, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>, and <i>Solanum lycopersicum</i> genes and separately to all Uniprot proteins. Similarity was detected with BLASTX of <i>Genlisea aurea</i> contigs against predicted proteomes of these organisms/Uniprot proteomes. In the cases of overlapping predictions the longest gene was taken. Second, we used transcribed sequences of closely related species <i>Utricularia intermedia</i> and <i>Pinguicula vulgaris</i> to predict genes in <i>Genlisea aurea</i> with GENESEQER [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Brendel V, Xing L, Zhu W: Gene structure prediction from consensus spliced alignment of multiple ESTs matching the same genomic locus. Bioinformatics. 2004, 20: 1157-1169. 10.1093/bioinformatics/bth058." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1972">69</a>]. Third, we performed ab initio similarity based gene prediction with AUGUSTUS [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Stanke M, Diekhans M, Baertsch R, Haussler D: Using native and syntenically mapped cDNA alignments to improve de novo gene finding. Bioinformatics. 2008, 24: 637-644. 10.1093/bioinformatics/btn013." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1976">70</a>] v.2.5.5. with gene model trained on 94 genes selected from genes predicted by previous two methods. Each selected gene should have similar protein in Uniprot with 95% coverage of amino acid sequences of both proteins by hit region. “--UTR = off” parameter was used for training procedure. As an input data for prediction by Augustus the hint-files were made using BLAT for alignment on the genome contigs the data from 454 transcriptome sequencing of <i>Utricularia gibba</i>, the species from sister genus <i>Utricularia</i> ([<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Ibarra-Laclette E, Albert VA, Pérez-Torres CA, Zamudio-Hernández F, de J Ortega-Estrada M, Herrera-Estrella A, Herrera-Estrella L: Transcriptomics and molecular evolutionary rate analysis of the bladderwort (Utricularia), a carnivorous plant with a minimal genome. BMC Plant Biol. 2011, 11: 101-10.1186/1471-2229-11-101." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1985">21</a>], SRA accession number SRR094438) and proteins from 20 plant genomes available in PlantGDB [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Duvick J, Fu A, Muppirala U, Sabharwal M, Wilkerson MD, Lawrence CJ, Lushbough C, Brendel V: PlantGDB: a resource for comparative plant genomics. Nucleic Acids Res. 2008, 36: D959-D965." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d2440e1988">10</a>] on March 2012. These are <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> (annotation version TAIR10), <i>Brachypodium distachyon</i> (192), <i>Brassica rapa</i> (197), <i>Carica papaya</i> (113), <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i> (169), <i>Cucumis sativus</i> (JGI1.0), <i>Glycine max</i> (109), <i>Lotus japonicus</i> (Kazusa1.0), <i>Manihot esculenta</i> (147), <i>Mimulus guttatus</i> (140), <i>Oryza sativa</i> (MSU7.0), <i>Physcomitrella patens</i> (152), <i>Prunus persica</i> (139), <i>Populus trichocarpa</i> (156), <i>Sorghum bicolor</i> (79), <i>Setaria italica</i> (164), <i>Solanum lycopersicum</i> (ITAG2), <i>Selaginella moellendorffii</i> (91), <i>Volvox carteri</i> (199), <i>Zea mays</i> (5b.60). Fourth, ab initio self-training gene prediction method GeneMark-ES [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Ter-Hovhannisyan V, Lomsadze A, Chernoff YO, Borodovsky M: Gene prediction in novel fungal genomes using an ab initio algorithm with unsupervised training. Genome Res. 2008, 18: 1979-1990. 10.1101/gr.081612.108." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2055">71</a>] was used with parameter “--min_contig 10000”.</p><p>Finally, we took the union of these seven annotations (1 – AUGUSTUS, 4 – GENEWISE, 2 – GENESEQER, 1 - GeneMark-ES). In the case of overlapping genes we took one with the best hit in Uniprot or in <i>M. guttatus</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, or <i>O. sativa</i>. If there was no significant hit for any of overlapping predictions, we took the longest one. Number of genes predicted with each program and overall number of genes in the final set are listed in Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#Tab1">1</a>. To search Pfam-domains all predicted genes were scanned with PfamScan on database Pfam-A v.26 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Mistry J, Bateman A, Finn R: Predicting active site residue annotations in the Pfam database. BMC Bioinforma. 2007, 8: 298-10.1186/1471-2105-8-298." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2077">72</a>]. To identify the clusters of orthologous genes, OrthoMCL [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Li L, Stoeckert CJ, Roos DS: OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 2003, 13: 2178-2189. 10.1101/gr.1224503." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2080">73</a>] was run on five plant genomes: <i>G. aurea, M. guttatus, A. thaliana, S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>.</p><p>To perform Gene Ontology annotation we used BLAST2GO [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Conesa A, Götz S: Blast2GO: A Comprehensive suite for functional analysis in plant genomics. Int J Plant Genomics. 2008, 2008: 1-12." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2092">9</a>]. Using predicted transcript set as a query BLAST was run with the e-value cut-off 10<sup>-3</sup> and the annotation with e-value cut-off 10<sup>-5</sup>. To provide a summary of the results of GO annotation of <i>Genlisea</i> genome plant GO-slim categories developed by TAIR were used. GOstat [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Beißbarth T, Speed TP: GOstat: find statistically overrepresented Gene Ontologies within a group of genes. Bioinformatics. 2004, 20: 1464-1465. 10.1093/bioinformatics/bth088." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2102">74</a>] was used to find statistically overrepresented and underrepresented gene ontologies.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Test of the assembly and gene number estimates</h3><p>The data on <i>Arabidopsis</i> genome were generated using the same experimental protocols as those of <i>Genlisea</i>. 50 millions of paired 100 bp reads were used for assembly. Two datasets were used: “clean” – containing only <i>Arabidopsis</i> reads and “contaminated”. To generate the latter, we performed a back-mapping of all reads used for assembly of <i>Genlisea</i> genome on filtered contigs (mapping parameters: aligned length 0.8, similarity 0.95) and collected the reads that did not map. These reads were added to <i>Arabidopsis</i> sequence data and assembled. Assembly was performed using CLC Genomics Workbench 6.0 with the same parameters as for assembly of <i>Genlisea</i> genome; the same was done with clean Arabidopsis reads. After assembly we analyzed coverage distribution for the assemblies of clean and contaminated datasets and removed from the contaminated assembly contigs with low coverage (less than 40×). Then contigs of both datasets were aligned on reference chromosomes of TAIR10 assembly by BLAT. All hits shorter than 1,000 bp (either in contigs or in chromosomes) and with identity below 90% were removed. All matched regions in reference chromosomes were joined to avoid hit overlapping. After that genes of reference annotation were tested for coverage by contigs of both datasets. Gene was classified as covered in case at least 50% of it was covered.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Calculating phylogenetic distances</h3><p>For each <i>G. aurea</i> gene we searched with BLAST for the best homologous gene in <i>M. guttatus</i> and <i>S. lycopersicum</i> genomes and <i>U. intermedia</i> and <i>P. vulgaris</i> transcriptomes. We obtained 8,677 groups of homologous genes, which are present in each of these 5 organisms. Then, each group of homologous genes was aligned with MACSE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Ranwez V, Harispe S, Delsuc F, Douzery EJP: MACSE: multiple alignment of coding SEquences accounting for frameshifts and stop codons. PLoS One. 2011, 6: e22594-10.1371/journal.pone.0022594." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2157">75</a>]. Finally, the concatenate of alignments was used to calculate synonymous and nonsynonymous distances with codeml program from PAML package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Yang Z: PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput Appl Biosci. 1997, 13: 555-556." href="/articles/10.1186/1471-2164-14-476#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d2440e2160">76</a>]. Only codon columns present in each 5 species were used in the analysis, <i>S. lycopersicum</i> sequence was used to root the tree.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Data access</h3><p>Annotated genome of <i>G. aurea</i> is available in the Genbank under BioProject accession number PRJNA208769. Data from other species generated in this study are available under BioProject accession number PRJNA211836.</p></div></div></section>
